deck, horrible browser</span></a></div><span class="a-color-secondary">              <span class="a-size-normal">     <span class="a-color-secondary">       By     </span>     <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A3U5HIO1T0155/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp" class="noTextDecoration">Joseph D. Brown</a>   </span> <span class="a-declarative" data-action="cr-popup" data-cr-popup="{&quot;width&quot;:340,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;AmazonHelp&quot;,&quot;height&quot;:340}" style="display:inline;"></span><span class="a-color-secondary"> on February 26, 2014</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R1XPPA8R5SLA4A" class="a-row a-spacing-small">      <div class="a-section">   This treadmill gets a solid 4 stars for the treadmill features. It gets dinged 1 star for the inability to display speed in miles/min (wth?) and another two stars for the unbelievably horrible browser. It has zero memory, doesn't remember cookies, and restarts itself when you start the treadmill, meaning you can't log in to a site like pandora or last.fm before starting your workout. video also plays at full screen resolution so last.fm is useless if you want to know how far you've run. the lack of memory and old android version are so bad that even the default sites - msnbc, fox, abc - don't really work. really ruins the experience and calls into question why it even has internet capability.
